    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer15937954005463405699"><i>Librarian's note: An alternate cover edition can be found <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/53769761.here' title='here' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a></i><br/><br/><b>No one’s ever told Eleanor that life should be better than fine</b><br/><br/>Meet Eleanor Oliphant: she struggles with appropriate social skills and tends to say exactly what she’s thinking. Nothing is missing in her carefully timetabled life of avoiding unnecessary human contact, where weekends are punctuated by frozen pizza</span>
  <span id="freeText15937954005463405699" style="display:none"><i>Librarian's note: An alternate cover edition can be found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/53769761.here" title="here" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a></i><br /><br /><b>No one’s ever told Eleanor that life should be better than fine</b><br /><br />Meet Eleanor Oliphant: she struggles with appropriate social skills and tends to say exactly what she’s thinking. Nothing is missing in her carefully timetabled life of avoiding unnecessary human contact, where weekends are punctuated by frozen pizza, vodka, and phone chats with Mummy. <br /><br />But everything changes when Eleanor meets Raymond, the bumbling and deeply unhygienic IT guy from her office. When she and Raymond together save Sammy, an elderly gentleman who has fallen, the three rescue one another from the lives of isolation that they had been living. Ultimately, it is Raymond’s big heart that will help Eleanor find the way to repair her own profoundly damaged one. If she does, she'll learn that she, too, is capable of finding friendship—and even love—after all.<br /><br />Smart, warm, uplifting, <i>Eleanor Oliphant Is Completely Fine</i> is the story of an out-of-the-ordinary heroine whose deadpan weirdness and unconscious wit make for an irresistible journey as she realizes. . . <br /> <br /><b>the only way to survive is to open your heart.</b></span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1091467-is-eleanor-an-aspie-or-on-the-spectrum-at">Is Eleanor an Aspie? Or on the Spectrum at all?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1091467'><a id="like_count_community_question_1091467" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1091467?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">228 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F31434883-eleanor-oliphant-is-completely-fine">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/82748043-melody-rule"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1575662969i/82748043._UY100_CR12,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/82748043-melody-rule">Melody Rule</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">As someone who has a professional diagnosis of autism which I finally received in my 40s I have been most upset by some comments. Every single autisti<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">As someone who has a professional diagnosis of autism which I finally received in my 40s I have been most upset by some comments. Every single autistic person is as different and individual as neurotypicals. I would never assume that all neurotypicals are good at social skills or enjoy physical contact just because they aren't Autistic. To suggest Eleanor cant be autistic because she likes holding hands is innacurate. I love to hold my husband's hand or my daughter's hand (Yes, shock horror, I am autistic, married and have a non autistic child!!) However, if a stranger were to touch me or even stand slightly close to me it would cause me huge anxiety. If my husband took my hand unexpectedly I would flinch. All behaviours can vary from day to day as with any human being. External factors as well as the autism itself have a bearing on how my traits present themselves. Also, Austism and it's huge range of traits and behaviours are measured on a spectrum and not a linear scale from severe to high functioning.<br /><br />To suggest its used as an excuse is incredibly insulting. Getting a proffessional diagnosis is an extremely difficult process (especially as an adult) often taking years so to suggest there is some kind of bandwagon is extremely ignorant and ill informed. It took months of interviews with various teams of professionals, my whole family had to be interviewed so they could be sure my issues had been since infancy and I had to get all my old school whixh was almost impossible.<br />My experience is that autism is not over diagnosed but in fact under diagnosed especially in women The diagnostic criteria they use is based on males who often present as having more classic signs than girls. <br />Many autistic people have been victims of abuse and suffer ptsd as a result of being bullied, lonely and living their whole lives feeling disconnected and confused by the world. PtSD and autism are far from being mutually exclusive. IF YOU'VE MET ONE PERSON WITH AUTISM YOU ONLY HAVE ONE EXPERIENCE OF AUTISM. <br />It makes me so sad (Yes, I feel emotions very deeply as many autistic people do) that in an age of so-called autism awareness that there is still so much misinformation and ignorance. I hope my post goes some way to dispell some very damaging myths<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I LOVE THIS ENDING. It leaves you with a sense of discouragement and hope at the same time--discouragement that Eleanor's issues are so much deeper th<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I LOVE THIS ENDING. It leaves you with a sense of discouragement and hope at the same time--discouragement that Eleanor's issues are so much deeper than she could've imagined, and hope that she now has a friend and a counselor to get her though it. Gave me chills.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_1996400398" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1996400398" />
    <a title="Deanna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15662887-deanna"><img alt="Deanna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437589889p2/15662887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1996400398?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna " href="/user/show/15662887-deanna">Deanna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780143199090" href="/book/show/32622051-eleanor-oliphant-is-completely-fine">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=highly-recommended">highly-recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=giveaways">giveaways</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=my-favorites">my-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1996400398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8319209712025420189">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com'>https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br/><br/>ALL THE STARS !!!<br/><br/>I won an advanced copy of this book through a Goodreads giveaway. Thank you!<br/><br/>To be honest, I'm not sure if this book would have been on my radar if I hadn't won it. Although the great reviews may have pulled me in. At any rate, I am so happy I read it.<br/><br/>I LOVED THIS BOOK !!<br/><br/>Just like it says in the title of the book, Eleanor Oliphant is completely fine....well she thinks she is. She is honestly not worried that </span>
  <span id="freeText8319209712025420189" style="display:none">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com">https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br /><br />ALL THE STARS !!!<br /><br />I won an advanced copy of this book through a Goodreads giveaway. Thank you!<br /><br />To be honest, I'm not sure if this book would have been on my radar if I hadn't won it. Although the great reviews may have pulled me in. At any rate, I am so happy I read it.<br /><br />I LOVED THIS BOOK !!<br /><br />Just like it says in the title of the book, Eleanor Oliphant is completely fine....well she thinks she is. She is honestly not worried that she may be missing out on anything. She is content with her life.<br /><br />Eleanor is a little bit....odd. She's very intelligent and well-spoken with impeccable grammar (thanks to Mummy) but she lacks the ability to filter what she says and therefore she will tell you exactly what she's thinking. This can lead to very awkward situations.<br /><br />Eleanor is comfortable with her routines. She's worked at the same job for nine years. She starts work at 8:30, at lunch she buys a newspaper which she reads from cover to cover and then does the crossword. She finishes out her day, leaving work at 5:30. Eleanor listens to the Archers as she makes a simple dinner (usually pasta and salad - one pan one plate), watches TV or reads for a little while then off to bed at ten. Her weekday routine only changes on Wednesday when she talks with "Mummy" for ten minutes. <br /><br />Weekends are a bit different. After work Friday she picks up pizza, wine and two big bottles of Vodka for the weekend. She drinks the vodka over the weekend.....in a state where she's neither drunk nor sober, waiting for Monday to come. No one comes over and she doesn't go anywhere to visit. She sometimes wonders if she's a figment of her own imagination.<br /><br />But she's fine with it. She's fine. There's nothing missing, she doesn't need anyone else. Well that was what she told herself. But then it happens...<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>"He was light and heat. He blazed. Everything he came into contact with would be changed. I sat forward on my seat, edged closer. At last. I found him"</em>
</strong><br /><br />Now Eleanor is on a mission. First she decides a make-over is in order....and where she starts is both shocking and hilarious. I really want to write about what happened but I think I would spoil a very funny moment for many readers.<br /><br />Things don't go exactly as planned.<br /><br />When her computer at work stops working she meets Raymond from IT. An easy-going guy, Raymond is intrigued by Eleanor, but she's just not interested. She's busy trying to re-create herself for the man of her dreams. But after work one day Eleanor and Raymond come across a man who has fallen on the sidewalk. Together they help the man, Sammy and so begins a friendship along with the start of many changes in Eleanor's life.<br /><br />The story is told from Eleanor's point of view. We go along for the ride as she navigates her way through her life, learning to stand up for herself. But it won't be easy. Secrets and memories that have been tucked away for many years can be painful to remember.<br /><br />When you have trouble with social skills I can see how it would be easier to refrain from situations where things could go wrong so fast..... It would be easier being alone. As I mentioned there are many funny moments throughout the book. I really like how the author wrote these parts. I never felt like I was laughing AT Eleanor but at the things she said or the situations she ended up in. However, there are also many sad and painful moments. Times where I felt terrible for Eleanor.<br /><br />Some of the funniest parts came out of nowhere - the phone doesn't ring often but if telemarketers call Eleanor whispers "I know where you live" and hangs up. Often it was what she would be saying to herself that was funny.<br /><br />An incredible read that had me bouncing from one emotion to the next. The author did a tremendous job bringing these wonderfully unique characters to life.<br /><br />It's hard to believe this is the author's debut novel.<br /><br />There are so many words that can be used to describe this novel - hilarious , unique, heartwarming, heartbreaking, charming, hopeful, inspiring, and COMPLETELY unforgettable.<br /><br /><br />HIGHLY RECOMMENDED!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8319209712025420189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1996553093" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1996553093" />
    <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong"><img alt="Susanne  Strong" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583087410p2/4514828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1996553093?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susanne  Strong" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong">Susanne  Strong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781524749699" href="/book/show/35127681-eleanor-oliphant-is-completely-fine">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=2017-five-star-books">2017-five-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1996553093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1691922942562901217">5 Stars.<br/><b>“Eleanor Oliphant Is Completely Fine” but after finishing this novel, <u>I am not. </u> <br/><br/>I was completely unprepared for the life of Eleanor Oliphant and that of her ‘Mummy.” To be frank, I was ill-equipped to deal with it, much like Eleanor. And it wrecked me. </b><br/><br/>At thirty years-old, Eleanor Oliphant is alone in this world. She always has been, actually. In and out of foster care since she was a little girl, she has never been touched by anyone in a loving way and doesn’t even know what that would</span>
  <span id="freeText1691922942562901217" style="display:none">5 Stars.<br /><b>“Eleanor Oliphant Is Completely Fine” but after finishing this novel, <u>I am not. </u> <br /><br />I was completely unprepared for the life of Eleanor Oliphant and that of her ‘Mummy.” To be frank, I was ill-equipped to deal with it, much like Eleanor. And it wrecked me. </b><br /><br />At thirty years-old, Eleanor Oliphant is alone in this world. She always has been, actually. In and out of foster care since she was a little girl, she has never been touched by anyone in a loving way and doesn’t even know what that would feel like, but that’s ok. All of her physical needs are met, you see and she has never had any emotional needs. <br /><br />Seeing as she doesn’t have any friends, Eleanor is quiet and socially awkward. Everyone thinks she is fairly strange, if you must to know. Not that she minds since people’s behavior makes absolutely no sense to her. She is good at being alone and she does not feel sorry for herself. Not even when ‘Mummy’ calls and viciously tells her daughter off and berates her for being being “naughty.” Eleanor, however wears a coat of armor and does her best to let her mother’s words bounce off of her. <br /><br />Eleanor has no aspirations though she has done accounting at an office for the last 9 years. Every day of her life is the same and she would be nothing without routine. One night, all of that changes rather abruptly. After work, she and a coworker named Raymond whom she just met and who happens to be leaving the office at the same time as her, find themselves in the exact right place at the right time. Both Eleanor and Raymond see a man (named Samuel), go down on the sidewalk and they go have a look see and discover that he needs an ambulance. This incident ends up tying the three together and becomes one of the most significant in Eleanor Oliphant’s life. It forges a bond of friendship between them, which is something Eleanor has never experienced before in all her thirty years. <br /><br />During this time, Eleanor also ends up finding him. The man she has been waiting for all of her life. The man she is meant to be with. Now she just has to get him to notice her. In trying to do so, Eleanor grows bolder and more confident. She also learns to lean on and open herself up to her new friends.<br /><br />Throughout the book, Eleanor slowly experiences a metamorphosis, one that often makes you smile, laugh and of course, cry. She is damaged and quirky but oh so special. I loved her dearly. For more reasons than one. I identified with Eleanor Oliphant you see, and for that, I was unprepared. I did say that this book wrecked me right?! I get why Eleanor is Completely Fine. She had no choice. Unfortunately, Eleanor’s ‘Mummy’ is someone I recognized fairly well. When I heard her voice (in a Scottish accent) on the audiobook, and the way she spoke to her daughter, my chest got tight and my throat closed up and I sobbed. Unlike Eleanor's “Mummy” however, mine happens to be British instead of Scottish - though the accents are close, thus I therefore guess that listening to the audiobook had an even more profound effect on me. I’ve had similar conversations, in case it wasn’t obvious and I felt Eleanor’s pain more deeply as it related to her ‘Mummy’, for at certain times in my life, it mirrored my own. All that aside however, Eleanor does not go quietly into the dark goodnight (and neither did I, for what it’s worth). <br /><br /><b>Though it affected me greatly, “Eleanor Oliphant is Completely Fine” is without a doubt one of the most incredible, profound, and beautifully well written novels I have absorbed in ages. It wrecked me in the best and worst ways possible. In case it’s not obvious, it will stay with me for a long time. I think I came across it on purpose as both Eleanor Oliphant and I needed something from it and I think we were both lucky enough to receive it. </b> <br /><br />Published on Goodreads and Amazon on 6.26.17.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1691922942562901217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2061111819" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2061111819" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2061111819?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2061111819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13842023605951693872">Eleanor Oliphant is completely 100% fine. She goes to her office job five days a week and then treats herself to a frozen pizza and a bottle of vodka on a weekend. She lives alone and doesn't have any friends, but that's okay. She's doing real well, thank you very much. <br/><br/>Except maybe she isn't. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31434883.Eleanor_Oliphant_is_Completely_Fine' title='Eleanor Oliphant is Completely Fine by Gail Honeyman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eleanor Oliphant is Completely Fine</a> caught me completely unawares. I'll be honest - I picked it up because it got some buzz and the author is British, but it actually turned out to be one of those <b>perfectl</b></span>
  <span id="freeText13842023605951693872" style="display:none">Eleanor Oliphant is completely 100% fine. She goes to her office job five days a week and then treats herself to a frozen pizza and a bottle of vodka on a weekend. She lives alone and doesn't have any friends, but that's okay. She's doing real well, thank you very much. <br /><br />Except maybe she isn't. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31434883.Eleanor_Oliphant_is_Completely_Fine" title="Eleanor Oliphant is Completely Fine by Gail Honeyman" rel="nofollow noopener">Eleanor Oliphant is Completely Fine</a> caught me completely unawares. I'll be honest - I picked it up because it got some buzz and the author is British, but it actually turned out to be one of those <b>perfectly-balanced sad/funny books</b>. Maybe like some combination of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16181775.The_Rosie_Project__Don_Tillman___1_" title="The Rosie Project (Don Tillman, #1) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Project</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_" title="Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23305614.Finding_Audrey" title="Finding Audrey by Sophie Kinsella" rel="nofollow noopener">Finding Audrey</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18774964.A_Man_Called_Ove" title="A Man Called Ove by Fredrik Backman" rel="nofollow noopener">A Man Called Ove</a>. It takes a serious, traumatic issue and weaves it into a warm, funny and, yes, sometimes sad tale.<br /><br />I read a lot of books and many characters come and go. Some are well-developed and interesting, others less so. But on a rare occasion I find one of those truly memorable characters that will stay with me a long time. Eleanor is one of them. She is <b>socially clueless</b> in a way that puts my teen self to shame. She is literal to a degree that everyone finds odd. It's painful to witness and yet so, so endearing.<br /><br />I think I like this book so much because it is actually really sad, but never manipulative. On a surface level, it's a very funny novel about a socially-inept twenty-nine year-old woman. Her attempts to become "normal" and integrate into society by having manicures and waxes are sources of hilarity. But it is very sad. It's sad when we see her coworkers talking about her, but Eleanor is oblivious to their scorn. It's sad how alone in life she is. It's sad when she "falls in love" with an idea of a person.<br /><br />It's not a romantic book and I'm glad. There are hints that the central relationship will eventually develop into romance, but this is really a book about Eleanor. I am thankful that the author didn't cure Eleanor and lead her out of the darkness by having her fall in love. Being happy and achieving greater self-worth should, in my opinion, never be linked to romance.<br /><br />I really enjoyed it. It's great to find a book so packed full of emotion without seeming overly-sentimental.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13842023605951693872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2586774069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7927501936931679633"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605371177i/30377107._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Need a good read for a bad day?   <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544495490i/26725700._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <i>If someone asks you how you are, you are meant to say FINE. You are not meant to say that you cried yourself to sleep last night because you hadn't spoken to another person for two consecutive days. FINE is what you say.</i>
</blockquote><b>Ohhh, I could not wish for a more perfect book.</b><br/><br/>Eleanor Oliphant is an office manager at a company. She's worked there for years and yet...<b>she's never fit in.</b><br/><br/>The other girls </span>
  <span id="freeText7927501936931679633" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605371177i/30377107._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Need a good read for a bad day? Here's a <u><b><a href="https://youtu.be/-GuEMAaGS3I" rel="nofollow noopener">Booktube Video</a> </b></u> all about it!!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>

  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544495490i/26725700._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>If someone asks you how you are, you are meant to say FINE. You are not meant to say that you cried yourself to sleep last night because you hadn't spoken to another person for two consecutive days. FINE is what you say.</i>
</blockquote><b>Ohhh, I could not wish for a more perfect book.</b><br><br>Eleanor Oliphant is an office manager at a company. She's worked there for years and yet...<b>she's never fit in.</b><br><br>The other girls at the office like to<b> whisper and giggle</b> - oftentimes at Eleanor - and the rest of them just think she's plain weird.<blockquote>
  <i>These days, loneliness is the new cancer – a shameful, embarrassing thing, brought upon yourself in some obscure way. </i>
</blockquote> But all that changes when she meets Raymond, an IT guy at the office.<br><br><b>They certainly don't hit it off,</b> but they do have a connection of sorts. <br><br>Raymond manages to get a peek at what's underneath Eleanor's shell...and he might just be able to pull her back before she really goes too far.<blockquote>
  <i>I have been waiting for death all my life. I do not mean that I actively wish to die, just that I do not really want to be alive.</i>
</blockquote><b>Whew. </b>After reading this one - I feel like I need to sleep for a week!<br><br>Gail Honeyman<b> expertly weaves </b>a story steeped with humor and love. <br><br>Eleanor was such an off-the-wall character - never over the top, but always just enough to be<b> an absolute delight.</b> <blockquote>
  <i>LOL could go and take a running jump. I wasn’t made for illiteracy; it simply didn’t come naturally.</i>
</blockquote>I adored Raymond's gentle prying and Eleanor's slow acceptance of other people. <br><br><b>This story is just so perfect </b>- everyone needs to pick up their copy - Right. Now.<blockquote>
  <i>In the end, what matters is this: I survived.</i>

<div id="review_1975539336" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1975539336" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5211606-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505571524p2/5211606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1975539336?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/5211606-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5211606-julie?shelf=don-t-believe-the-hype">don-t-believe-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5211606-julie?shelf=nobody-talks-like-this">nobody-talks-like-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5211606-julie?shelf=100-pages-too-long">100-pages-too-long</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1975539336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9169022533662806604">No. No. No. No. No. No.<br/><br/>All apologies to my lovely Goodreads friends who have liked (or loved) this book, but it's not for me. <br/><br/>And it's sad. . . because I wanted it, I waited for it, and I was finally able to start it. It's Mother's Day, and my family handed me bath salts and my new book and told me to go for it. They know I'm just crazy enough to read an entire book in one bath, and I was ready to do it.<br/><br/>And I prepared my bath, and I began reading, and I was (very quickly) almost in physical pain</span>
  <span id="freeText9169022533662806604" style="display:none">No. No. No. No. No. No.<br /><br />All apologies to my lovely Goodreads friends who have liked (or loved) this book, but it's not for me. <br /><br />And it's sad. . . because I wanted it, I waited for it, and I was finally able to start it. It's Mother's Day, and my family handed me bath salts and my new book and told me to go for it. They know I'm just crazy enough to read an entire book in one bath, and I was ready to do it.<br /><br />And I prepared my bath, and I began reading, and I was (very quickly) almost in physical pain. I don't mean to be rude to the author; I know how hard it is to write a novel and get it published, but this would not have made it past my eyes, if she had handed it to me.<br /><br />Again, ALL APOLOGIES, but this is Mother's Day, and you have one annoyed mother on your hands. You have ruined my bath, and in doing so, you have released the Kraken!! <br /><br />MUST the reader be invited in to experience every one of Eleanor's bowel movements and meals? MUST we suffer through every not-interesting-in-the-least observation on life?<br /><br />And, how must we EVER believe that a woman this bizarre would be able to function in the world and/or experience a friendship or a romance? <br /><br />According to Eleanor, she has "white contours of scar tissue that slither across my right cheek." Here's where I just about threw the book. Explain. No, seriously. Explain how scar tissue slithers across a face. Do you mean as you are speaking or making funny faces? Did you attend Hogwarts? Are you a Slytherin? Help, please!<br /><br />Also. . . somehow. . . Eleanor hangs up phones quietly. But, it's 2017, and we all just use that little button now. There's no loud, there's no quiet, there's just that one button. Explain.<br /><br />Oh, and when she hangs up the phone with her Mummy (choke and gag), "It was only when the air went dead that I noticed I'd been crying."<br /><br />How does the air go dead? No, I'm not kidding. Please, explain what that sounds like, what it looks like. How does the air go dead?<br /><br />If you want to read about a WAY more adorable person with Asperger's. . . go find Don Tillman. If you want to read about a WAY more delightful curmudgeon, go find Olive Kitteridge.<br /><br />I saved myself from drowning by stopping at page 50.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9169022533662806604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2041801702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8499897690030875151">4.5! What an incredible story!<br/><br/><i> “These days, loneliness is the new cancer - a shameful, embarrassing thing, brought upon yourself in some obscure way. A fearful, incurable thing, so horrifying that you dare not mention it; other people don’t want to hear the word spoken aloud for fear that they might too be afflicted.” </i><br/><br/>Eleanor’s story hit me so much harder than I expected it to. She is thirty years old, has worked at the same job since she left university, speaks on the phone to mummy once a week</span>
  <span id="freeText8499897690030875151" style="display:none">4.5! What an incredible story!<br /><br /><i> “These days, loneliness is the new cancer - a shameful, embarrassing thing, brought upon yourself in some obscure way. A fearful, incurable thing, so horrifying that you dare not mention it; other people don’t want to hear the word spoken aloud for fear that they might too be afflicted.” </i><br /><br />Eleanor’s story hit me so much harder than I expected it to. She is thirty years old, has worked at the same job since she left university, speaks on the phone to mummy once a week and drinks two litres of vodka every weekend. Eleanor Oliphant is fine. <br /><br />One day, Eleanor and a colleague help assist an elderly man who’d fallen over on the street. From there we follow Eleanor and Raymond’s budding friendship, and we realise just how ‘not fine’ Eleanor truly is. <br /><br /><i> “I’d tried so hard, but something about me just didn’t fit. There was, it seemed, no Eleanor-shaped social hole for me to slot into.” </i><br /><br />Eleanor is painfully relatable, her awkwardness at social encounters, reliance on alcohol and the burying of all feelings and past grievances, is something I feel on a personal level. It’s as if her story came to me at just the right time in my life. It was heartbreaking, honest and powerful. <br /><br /><i> “I was thirty years old, I realised, and I had never walked hand in hand with anyone. No one had ever rubbed my tired shoulders, or stroked my face.” </i><br /><br />All of us have felt alone at some point in our lives, Eleanor’s story serves as a reminder that we are a lot more alike than we realise. A bit of kindness can go such a long way, friendship can truly be life saving.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8499897690030875151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2162075416" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2162075416" />
    <a title="j e w e l s" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s"><img alt="j e w e l s" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552606306p2/68216634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2162075416?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="j e w e l s" class="user" itemprop="url" name="j e w e l s" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s">j e w e l s</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/32503381-eleanor-oliphant-is-completely-fine">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2162075416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7026356445109066180"><b>5 STARS</b><br/><br/>Thank you, Eleanor Oliphant. Thank you for picking me up out of my reading slump. Thank you for being so funny, so sad, so smart, so blunt. Thank you for being a literary character that will live forever in the hearts of (most) anyone that reads you. <br/><br/>Oh, and a big thank you for enriching my own personal vocab. My Kindle dictionary has never had such a workout. What a nice perk!! Effortless writing that flows naturally fast, even though Eleanor O prefers to use crossword type clues as actu</span>
  <span id="freeText7026356445109066180" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS</b><br /><br />Thank you, Eleanor Oliphant. Thank you for picking me up out of my reading slump. Thank you for being so funny, so sad, so smart, so blunt. Thank you for being a literary character that will live forever in the hearts of (most) anyone that reads you. <br /><br />Oh, and a big thank you for enriching my own personal vocab. My Kindle dictionary has never had such a workout. What a nice perk!! Effortless writing that flows naturally fast, even though Eleanor O prefers to use crossword type clues as actual everyday language. She is a piece of work! And I adore her.<br /><br />I didn’t want this book to end. No, seriously did not want it to end, so why did I devour it as fast as ice cream melting at a picnic? Because it is that good! My black, black heart doesn't always have to read about murders and mysteries. I love a feel good story as much as the next guy. I just need it to be the right kind of writing <b>(GOOD, NOT cheesy).</b> The right kind of character <b>(layered, quirky, UNIQUE). </b> I have to admit, I wasn't a huge fan of A MAN CALLED OVE. Ove did not strike me as a real person. He felt artificial and a bit contrived. Made up. Eleanor O, on the other hand, is real.<br /><br />This is the right kind of everything. Thank you, Ms. Honeyman, for writing it. I actually feel sad for other books that try so hard to achieve the big feels and don't even come close to Eleanor Oliphant. <br /><br /><i>I've meant to read this for at least a year now and finally was nudged into it by my bookclub IRL! If this is on your TBR and you haven't read it yet, ahhhhhhh, I envy you. Don't wait a minute longer. Do it now!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7026356445109066180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2582408069" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2582408069" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528750408p2/9684061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2582408069?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=unforgettable-reads">unforgettable-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2582408069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1037011394858273106">As you can deduce from the title, Eleanor Oliphant is completely <u>fine</u>. Or, so <i>she</i> thinks. But, by most people’s standards, I’d say not.<br/><br/>When you first meet her, it’s hard not to feel overwhelmingly sad for Eleanor. Maybe even to pity her a bit. <b>Eleanor is simply existing</b> in a lonely and somber life without friends or family. And let’s be honest, at times her bluntness is sort of off-putting.<br/><br/>Eleanor is just <u>fine</u> living by her own self-imposed routine. The hour-long lunch spent with the same sandwi</span>
  <span id="freeText1037011394858273106" style="display:none">As you can deduce from the title, Eleanor Oliphant is completely <u>fine</u>. Or, so <i>she</i> thinks. But, by most people’s standards, I’d say not.<br /><br />When you first meet her, it’s hard not to feel overwhelmingly sad for Eleanor. Maybe even to pity her a bit. <b>Eleanor is simply existing</b> in a lonely and somber life without friends or family. And let’s be honest, at times her bluntness is sort of off-putting.<br /><br />Eleanor is just <u>fine</u> living by her own self-imposed routine. The hour-long lunch spent with the same sandwich and the daily crossword puzzle. The nightly pesto dinner recipe. The Friday treat of frozen pizza and wine. And the vodka, lots and lots of vodka—her coping mechanism for the long and lonesome weekends.<br /><br />The epitome of socially awkward, Eleanor is oblivious to social cues and norms, uninhibited by a filter, quite literal, and extremely frugal. At thirty, she’s set with her one and only job—no ambition for anything better or more challenging on the horizon.<br /><br />Laying eyes on “husband material” sparks her desire for a metamorphosis of sorts. She figures landing her soulmate is going to require some work—new hair, clothes and maybe even a little makeup to hide her facial scarring. After all, being with a musician requires a certain poise.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>There are scars on my heart, just as thick, as disfiguring as those on my face. I know they're there. I hope some undamaged tissue remains, a patch through with love can come in and flow out. I hope.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />It’s actually a happenstance run-in with one of her coworkers and the ensuing friendship that inspires the most change in Eleanor—her outlook on life and interactions with people. It’s comical that Raymond doesn’t seem fazed by Eleanor’s stunted social skills. In fact, his mellow attitude and companionship go a long way to smooth her edges.<br /><br />When things don’t go to plan, Eleanor is forced to stare down her truth. To succumb to the reality that <i>everyone</i> has problems and no feeling is insurmountable. That eventually with time—not vodka—things will get better. It's the <i>why</i> behind it all that broke my heart.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14558709.Gail_Honeyman" title="Gail Honeyman" rel="nofollow noopener"> Gail Honeyman</a> balances the heavy—and there’s a lot here, so be prepared—<b>with humor and hope</b>; taking readers on a journey right along with Eleanor. My own feelings skewing from odd to charmed. Quirky Eleanor managed to chip off a piece of my heart, stowing it away in her trusty shopper for safekeeping. <br /><br />With a pair of pom-poms in hand, I stood on the sidelines cheering Eleanor on as she discovered what life is truly about—<i>living</i>. Connecting with others. Taking those much-needed pauses to drink in her surroundings. And the potential for <i>more</i> in each and every aspect of life. From broken soul to a woman on a mission to live life, Eleanor's is an inspiring story, one I know I’m better for reading. <br /><br />And naturally, the part that squeezed the <i>awww</i> out of me—the healing powers of Glen. =^..^=</span>
  <a data-text-id="1037011394858273106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2451457637" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2451457637" />
    <a title="Paul Bryant" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/416390-paul-bryant"><img alt="Paul Bryant" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1224113172p2/416390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2451457637?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Bryant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Bryant" href="/user/show/416390-paul-bryant">Paul Bryant</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/416390-paul-bryant?shelf=novels">novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2451457637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18247731080668207301">Here is a novel at the exact room temperature everyone likes, not too cold, not to hot, just right, it’s like Goldilocks finding the right bed, everybody jumps in and goes right off to sleep, no one has a bad word to say, the Guardian loved it, the Irish Times said it “hits the accessible literary sweet spot”, Costa Book Prize, Reece Witherspoon to star in the movie, five stars rain down upon Eleanor Oliphant on Goodreads until she can no longer be seen, buried beneath tons of billowy love. If T</span>
  <span id="freeText18247731080668207301" style="display:none">Here is a novel at the exact room temperature everyone likes, not too cold, not to hot, just right, it’s like Goldilocks finding the right bed, everybody jumps in and goes right off to sleep, no one has a bad word to say, the Guardian loved it, the Irish Times said it “hits the accessible literary sweet spot”, Costa Book Prize, Reece Witherspoon to star in the movie, five stars rain down upon Eleanor Oliphant on Goodreads until she can no longer be seen, buried beneath tons of billowy love. If The Beatles could reform they would issue a single immediately called “All You Need is Eleanor Oliphant”. <br><br>Our story is a simple one. Eleanor is the poster girl for loneliness and social isolation caused by having a frightful childhood resulting in a truly traumatic event (no spoiler : a house fire). Eleanor is 30 and has zero friends, less than zero family, a poorly paid job, doesn’t speak to her co-workers, doesn’t even have a cat or a dog or a budgie or a little worm as a pet. Not even a little tiny worm! <br><br>Eleanor has a ridiculously pompous conversational style. So unfamiliar with normal human interaction is Eleanor that she has not realised that most people do not want to be spoken to as if they are in a posh drawing room in the 1950s. It’s like she has lived without tv or radio or newspapers or magazines or <i>anything</i>. <br><br>Example number one :<br><br><i>“Let us retire to an inn or public house, Raymond – a quiet one – and please, allow me to buy you some beer in recompense for this wasted evening.”</i><br><br>Example two :<br><br><i>“You don’t need to stay long – just show face; have a cup of tea, eat a sausage roll – you know the drill.” Said Raymond. <br>“Well I hope they’ve at least got a high meat content and friable pastry, “ I said.</i><br><br>Example three: when she gets a cat (oops, spoiler!) she says :<br><br><i>I will assume the mantle of care… This creature will be looked after assiduously.</i><br><br>Example four :<br><br><i>“You’re a good worker, Eleanor,” he said. “How long has it been now – eight years?”<br>“Nine,” I said.<br>“Nine years, and you’ve never had a day off sick, never used all your annual leave. That’s dedication, you know. It’s not easy to find these days.”<br>“It’s not dedication, “ I said. “I simply have a very robust constitution and no one to go on holiday with.”</i><br><br>Yes, it’s quite funny, but now, come on Gail Honeyman, no one is as loopy or brusque or unaware as that. Even Eleanor would know her remark was inappropriate, embarrassing, too much information – even if she meant it to be funny, which she didn’t, because, like any Vulcan, she has no sense of humour. She is the source of the humour but never understands why anyone is laughing. It did occur to me that Eleanor was somewhere on the autism spectrum but that is never alluded to in the novel. Has Gail Honeyman created an Asperger Syndrome character without realising it or is she just playing Eleanor for some pretty easy laughs? <br><br>As well as not knowing how real people talk to each other, Eleanor has no knowledge of popular culture. She has not heard of Laurel and Hardy (“the film was about a fat, clever man and a thin, stupid man who’d joined the Foreign Legion. They were patently unsuited to it”) ; and yet she namedrops J D Salinger and the Unabomber. She doesn’t know what parking meters are :<br><br><i>“I’ll need to run, Eleanor – the car’s on the meter and you know what those wardens are like if you go a minute over.”<br>I had absolutely no idea what she was talking about but I let it pass.</i><br><br>As you see there are some nice comedy moments. Here’s another favourite : we all know about product placement on tv and in movies. How about reverse-product placement? This is where you aggressively badmouth a specific item quite gratuitously. Eleanor is observing someone else’s basket of purchases in a supermarket :<br><br><i>Eggs, bacon, orange juice and Nurofen tablets. I had to stop myself from leaning forward and explaining that he was wasting his money – this branded non-steroidal anti-inflammatory drug was in fact ibuprofen 200 mg, the generic version of which was readily available for sale at perhaps one-quarter of the price. </i><br><br>For 70% of the time this novel is gentle comedy, of the sort you can find in sitcoms like <i>Not Going Out</i> or <i>The Vicar of Dibley</i> if the Vicar had a brain injury. But then begins the process of Eleanor thawing out and assuming a more “normal” shape. The great thing about this novel now emerges. This novel believes in <i>ordinary human kindness</i> as the thing which can save us, and <i>not romantic love</i>, and that is a great message which is very rarely heard. <br><br>But the normalising of Eleanor has some disturbing aspects. Quite often it’s like a rerun of Georgy Girl, the folksy hit by The Seekers from 1966.<br><br> <i> Hey there, Georgy girl<br> Swingin' down the street so fancy-free<br> Nobody you meet could ever see the loneliness there - inside you<br> Hey there, Georgy girl<br> Look at all the boyfriends you don’t get<br> Never had a real one yet, just look at the clothes you wear<br> You're always window shopping but never stopping to buy<br> Just shed those dowdy feathers and fly - a little bit</i><br><br>And the dowdy feathers are indeed shed – cue humorous sketches involving bikini waxes, new hairdos and new clothes. “But Miss Oliphant… you’re beautiful!” is almost said by at least two characters. <br><br>Well. I absolutely don’t want to kick this novel down the cellar steps and have it look back up at me all begrimed with cobwebs and sing "Where is Love?" through big blobby tears. I love the gospel of ordinary human kindness here, even though it’s wrapped up in some fairly disgraceful looksism and evangelical therapyspeak towards the end. I argued myself up down and sideways about Eleanor Oliphant and finally copped out with a rueful three stars. This is a nice novel. I should be nice to it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532272595i/26013421.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="18247731080668207301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2009342386" />
    <a title="Always Pouting" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting"><img alt="Always Pouting" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483476563p2/48650982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2009342386?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Always Pouting" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Always Pouting" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting">Always Pouting</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/32503381-eleanor-oliphant-is-completely-fine">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2009342386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13778222516436338203">Eleanor Oliphant lives a fairly secluded life due to her lack of social graces and crippling self esteem and anxiety issues. She works at a graphic design firm in the finance department and spends the rest of her time at home, usually drinking. Her social life consists of a phone call with her mummy every week. Then one day she goes to a concert, for which she won tickets in a raffle, and falls in love at first sight with a musician. Eleanor decides to make some changes to herself as part of a p</span>
  <span id="freeText13778222516436338203" style="display:none">Eleanor Oliphant lives a fairly secluded life due to her lack of social graces and crippling self esteem and anxiety issues. She works at a graphic design firm in the finance department and spends the rest of her time at home, usually drinking. Her social life consists of a phone call with her mummy every week. Then one day she goes to a concert, for which she won tickets in a raffle, and falls in love at first sight with a musician. Eleanor decides to make some changes to herself as part of a plan to get her dream man. Meanwhile a new hire in the IT department of her company, Raymond, strikes up a friendship with Eleanor. As things change for Eleanor she is forced to confront the past and confront the real reason for her recent desire for more. <br /><br />I really enjoyed this, oh man Eleanor is so quirky and endearing. Her inner monologue was excellent and I could really relate to her. I had an especially visceral reaction when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ she is at the concert and suddenly feels disgusted with herself when she realizes she's been projecting this whole time and created a fantasy in her head and just feels foolish  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> because come on who hasn't had a moment like that. I've had my fair share of moments when I try really hard and then just feel embarrassed and stupid about everything I've done. Eleanor just felt so real and human. The only thing that annoyed me was the ending when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ we find out her mother isn't alive she was imagining it  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> because it felt unnecessary and I didn't think we needed a plot twist like it kind of ruined all her conversations with her mom for me a little bit. Everything else was really great though, definitely 4.5 stars.</span>

<div id="review_2037130235" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2037130235" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2037130235?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2037130235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3497139741894336185">I'd rate this 4.5 stars.<br/><br/>I'll admit, when I started reading Gail Honeyman's debut novel, <b>
  <i>Eleanor Oliphant is Completely Fine</i>
</b>, I thought about issuing a moratorium on quirky characters who can't seem to pick up social cues or are oblivious to how people usually behave when interacting with peers, coworkers, those who provide service, and others. Obviously these are colorful characters to write about—it seems as if the literary world is full of them.<br/><br/>But the more time I spent with Eleanor Olipha</span>
  <span id="freeText3497139741894336185" style="display:none">I'd rate this 4.5 stars.<br><br>I'll admit, when I started reading Gail Honeyman's debut novel, <b>
  <i>Eleanor Oliphant is Completely Fine</i>
</b>, I thought about issuing a moratorium on quirky characters who can't seem to pick up social cues or are oblivious to how people usually behave when interacting with peers, coworkers, those who provide service, and others. Obviously these are colorful characters to write about—it seems as if the literary world is full of them.<br><br>But the more time I spent with Eleanor Oliphant, I realized that her behavior was more the result of circumstance than will, nurture if you will, rather than nature. And then I thought about how boring the world might be if everyone acted the way they were expected to, said the right things, and never expressed their true feelings. (Lord knows if I couldn't roll my eyes, my head might explode.)<br><br>Eleanor lives by her routines. She eats the same meals, wears the same clothes, has her weekly chat with Mummy, and has her weekend rituals, which include frozen pizza and enough vodka to keep her pleasantly drunk all weekend. For the most part, she eschews interactions with her coworkers, whom she mostly thinks are daft and lazy. They make fun of her both behind her back and in front of her, and she doesn't really care.<br><br>"I do not light up a room when I walk into it. No one longs to see me or hear my voice. I do not feel sorry for myself, not in the least. These are simply statements of fact."<br><br>Two things happen which throw her routines off-kilter. First, while attending a concert with a coworker, she spots a handsome musician and is quickly smitten. She has decided that he is the one for her, and starts to ready herself for their first encounter, during which she knows he'll sweep her off her feet and they'll live happily ever after. She needs a makeover and new clothes, and she starts doing research on her soon-to-be-beloved.<br><br>Meanwhile, one afternoon she and Raymond, the IT guy from her office, whom she considers poorly groomed and a bit bumbling, save the life of an elderly man who falls in front of them. Saving Sammy's life suddenly gives Eleanor two unexpected relationships, friendships, that she has never had before. She still acts the way she believes to be appropriate, and says things that most wouldn't, but she begins liking the feeling of belonging, of companionship, which she never realized she wanted.<br><br>"Some people, weak people, fear solitude. What they fail to understand is that there's something very liberating about it, once you realize that you don't need anyone, you can take care of yourself. That's the thing: it's <i>best</i> just to take care of yourself. You can't protect other people, however hard you try. You try, and you fail, and your world collapses around you, burns down to ashes."<br><br>Eleanor's social awkwardness, her lack of a filter, her inability to grasp exactly how people expect her to behave, actually hides a great deal of secret pain, pain and memories even she has hidden. And when she is forced to start recognizing just what a burden she has carried for so much of her life, and who was responsible, it threatens to break her. Suddenly she realizes she may need to do something she never has—depend on others, and reveal things about herself she's always kept hidden, in order to move forward. If she wants to.<br><br><b>
  <i>Eleanor Oliphant is Completely Fine</i>
</b> is really a special book. Even if some of Eleanor's behaviors are similar to other quirky characters you might have seen, she is totally unique, and while off-putting, just absolutely wonderful. You both marvel and are saddened by the burdens she has carried, and how she copes with them. I found myself becoming protective of her, worrying there would come an instant where someone made a total fool out of her (with her own help, of course).<br><br>Honeyman really did a terrific job with Eleanor. Even as she began letting down her guard, Honeyman kept her character consistent, but never let her become unsympathetic. While this is certainly Eleanor's story, I liked the other characters as well, although they certainly didn't get as much attention. I thought the ending was a little too pat for my taste, but I really enjoyed this overall, and don't think I'll be forgetting Eleanor or her story anytime soon.<br><br>God bless the people who challenge our notions of "appropriate" and "normal," because they are what keeps our world interesting!<br><br><div>
  <a href="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-O5Pl6wuUbB0/WU8UYP-SPtI/AAAAAAAAL9s/533N1H-EK8A1zGKPVNPuT08XnQ2RapgXgCLcBGAs/s1600/i_know_you_are_pee_wee_herman.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498355971ra/23118582.gif" width="320" height="174" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div></span>
  <a data-text-id="3497139741894336185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1992065551" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1992065551" />
    <a title="Diane S ☔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s"><img alt="Diane S ☔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598402138p2/4159922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1992065551?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane S ☔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane S ☔" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s">Diane S ☔</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1992065551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11071579943364674936">What an absolutely fantastic character Eleanor is, a character that grew on me the more I read. She has had a scarred childhood, though we don't learn exactly what happened until later in the story, she wears the evidence on her face. She remembers little from that time only knows she was burned in a fire. Raised in a series of group homes, given an apartment by social services who still check on her though she is now thirty. She has few social skills, is very matter of fact, has no friends, few</span>
  <span id="freeText11071579943364674936" style="display:none">What an absolutely fantastic character Eleanor is, a character that grew on me the more I read. She has had a scarred childhood, though we don't learn exactly what happened until later in the story, she wears the evidence on her face. She remembers little from that time only knows she was burned in a fire. Raised in a series of group homes, given an apartment by social services who still check on her though she is now thirty. She has few social skills, is very matter of fact, has no friends, few filters and has a schedule that she keeps to, a job she likes and insists she is fine. Until a crush with a musician and an IT guy named Raymond derails her schedule and her life.<br /><br />Why did I give this five stars? It is a first book, with nary a misstep, an assured book with amazing writing and character development. Plus it is difficult to take a book with so few characters, and not only make it interesting enough to keep the reader immersed, but to let us see the way Eleanor changes and grows throughout the story. There is much humor, there is also sadness and I came to embrace this character in all her strangeness, loved when she figured things out and came to terms with her past. There are a few places where the author could have gone overboard on sweetness but she kept true to the character of Eleanor and just managed to stay on the border, without crossing over. This is a book I will remember, it was that good and meaningful, in my opinion. <br /><br />Looking forward to great things from this new author, she is a true talent. <br />Thanks to my friend Esil who told me to grab this one.<br />ARC from publisher.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11071579943364674936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2685150383" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2685150383" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2685150383?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781524749699" href="/book/show/35127681-eleanor-oliphant-is-completely-fine">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Matthew by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/7115890-constantine">Constantine</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2685150383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18118157680660969534">Eleanor Oliphant is <b>NOT</b> completely fine!<br/><br/>Well, at least not at first!<br/><br/>This book is a fantastic character study. The journey with quirky Eleanor through the past and present is bizarre at times, thought-provoking at others. But, I found it to be engaging no matter what. And, while it is mainly about Eleanor, there are a few other interesting characters met along the way as well. Such a fun ride!<br/><br/>Also, I thought from the start of the book it was just going to be a general humor-fiction sort of book. </span>
  <span id="freeText18118157680660969534" style="display:none">Eleanor Oliphant is <b>NOT</b> completely fine!<br /><br />Well, at least not at first!<br /><br />This book is a fantastic character study. The journey with quirky Eleanor through the past and present is bizarre at times, thought-provoking at others. But, I found it to be engaging no matter what. And, while it is mainly about Eleanor, there are a few other interesting characters met along the way as well. Such a fun ride!<br /><br />Also, I thought from the start of the book it was just going to be a general humor-fiction sort of book. But, there are some very dark and twisted elements that are encountered along the way that put this book in a class/genre all by itself. I truly don't think I have ever seen a book that combines dark mystery and humor quite the same way that this book does.<br /><br />You know, when I sat down to write this, I thought I was going to go 4 stars. But, in writing the paragraphs above and thinking about the uniqueness of the story and how engaged I was with Eleanor's journey, I am going to have to up it to 5 stars.<br /><br />Give this one a try! While you may recognize some of the elements, I think in the end, as a whole, it is a totally new experience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18118157680660969534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1986603036" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1986603036" />
    <a title="Angela M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4685500-angela-m"><img alt="Angela M" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512600770p2/4685500.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1986603036?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela M" href="/user/show/4685500-angela-m">Angela M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1986603036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13641800249276017386">At first it’s easy to think that Eleanor is just a quirky social misfit with no friends and no social life and she is, but I soon found out that there is so much more to Eleanor and so much more to learn about her. It’s a lonely life she leads and she says everything is fine but we learn eventually that it isn’t, and that life hasn’t ever been fine. While hints of what happened to her are slowly divulged, we never really find out everything until the end . It’s heartbreaking to learn why she dro</span>
  <span id="freeText13641800249276017386" style="display:none">At first it’s easy to think that Eleanor is just a quirky social misfit with no friends and no social life and she is, but I soon found out that there is so much more to Eleanor and so much more to learn about her. It’s a lonely life she leads and she says everything is fine but we learn eventually that it isn’t, and that life hasn’t ever been fine. While hints of what happened to her are slowly divulged, we never really find out everything until the end . It’s heartbreaking to learn why she drowns herself in alcohol and fantasizes about a guy in a band, wanting a guy to love her, scars and all, the ones on the outside and those in her heart.<br /><br />Although, there is some humor to be found here, this really is such a profoundly sad story. I found it very difficult to read at times, especially hearing the disturbing things that she tells us her mother says to her in their weekly conversations. She’s ridiculed and laughed at by her coworkers except for the seemingly odd Raymond, the IT guy with whom she becomes friends. Suddenly Eleanor Is living parts of the life that her past had taken away from her. She slowly gets to know a little of the world that she had hidden herself from for so many years behind the walls of her apartment and large quantities of vodka. I’m almost at a loss for anything further to say, except that I’m sorry I waited so long to read this book. I didn’t get to it right away because I really thought it was just another quirky book and I couldn’t have been more wrong. It’s about how people can impact each other’s lives in unbearably awful ways and how others rise to save them. A fantastic debut that is not to be missed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13641800249276017386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
